## üõ†Ô∏è Installation & Setup (Beginner Friendly)

### ‚úÖ Step 1: Install Java 21 (OpenJDK)

1. Visit the official OpenJDK builds:
   üëâ [https://jdk.java.net/21/](https://jdk.java.net/21/)

2. Download the correct installer for your OS (Windows/Linux/macOS).

3. **Extract or Install** the JDK, then set environment variables:

#### ‚úÖ On Windows:

- Open *System Properties ‚Üí Environment Variables*
- Under **System Variables**, click **New**:
    - **Name**: JAVA_HOME
    - **Value**: C:\Program Files\Java\jdk-21 (adjust based on your path)
- Edit Path ‚Üí Add:
  %JAVA_HOME%\bin

Then confirm via terminal:

bash
java -version


Should return something like:
java 21 2023-09-19 ‚úîÔ∏è

---

### ‚úÖ Step 2: Clone the Repository

bash
git clone https://github.com/kyriakidisdimitrios/securityApi.git
cd securityApi


---

### ‚úÖ Step 3: Install & Configure MySQL

1. Install MySQL from:
   üëâ [https://dev.mysql.com/downloads/installer/](https://dev.mysql.com/downloads/installer/)

2. Create a new database:

sql
CREATE DATABASE bookstore;


3. Update your Spring config file src/main/resources/application.properties:

properties
spring.datasource.url=jdbc:mysql://localhost:3306/bookstore
spring.datasource.username=your_mysql_username
spring.datasource.password=your_mysql_password

spring.jpa.hibernate.ddl-auto=update
spring.jpa.show-sql=true
spring.jpa.properties.hibernate.dialect=org.hibernate.dialect.MySQLDialect


---

### ‚úÖ Step 4: Build and Run the Project

If you have Maven installed:

bash
mvn spring-boot:run


If you're using the wrapper (preferred):

bash
./mvnw spring-boot:run


Visit the app at:
üîó [http://localhost:8080](http://localhost:8080)

---

### ‚úÖ Note: Maven uses your Java environment

> Make sure your project **and Maven** use the same JDK version (Java 21).
You can verify Maven uses the correct Java by running:

bash
mvn -v


Ensure it outputs:
Java version: 21, vendor: Oracle Corporation (or OpenJDK)

Œ§Œø ChatGPT ŒµŒØœÄŒµ:
To safely delete all records from tables like customers, books, authors, book_authors, cart_items, etc., and bypass the "safe update mode" error in MySQL Workbench or similar tools, follow these three steps:

‚úÖ Step 1: Disable Safe Update Mode (Temporarily or Permanently)
Option A: Temporarily disable in session
Run this before executing DELETE statements:

sql
ŒëŒΩœÑŒπŒ≥œÅŒ±œÜŒÆ
ŒïœÄŒµŒæŒµœÅŒ≥Œ±œÉŒØŒ±
SET SQL_SAFE_UPDATES = 0;
Option B: Permanently disable in MySQL Workbench
Go to Edit ‚Üí Preferences ‚Üí SQL Editor

Uncheck ‚úÖ "Safe Updates"

Restart the MySQL Workbench session

‚úÖ Step 2: Delete Data in Correct Order (Respect Foreign Keys)
Assuming your database schema is named bookstore, and your foreign key constraints are properly defined, use this delete sequence:

sql
ŒëŒΩœÑŒπŒ≥œÅŒ±œÜŒÆ
ŒïœÄŒµŒæŒµœÅŒ≥Œ±œÉŒØŒ±
-- Step 1: Clear cart items first (they depend on customers and books)
DELETE FROM cart_items;

-- Step 2: Clear join table before deleting books or authors
DELETE FROM book_authors;

-- Step 3: Delete dependent entities
DELETE FROM books;
DELETE FROM authors;

-- Step 4: Finally, delete users/customers
DELETE FROM customers;
‚úÖ Step 3: (Optional) Reset Auto-Increment IDs
To start IDs again from 1:

sql
ŒëŒΩœÑŒπŒ≥œÅŒ±œÜŒÆ
ŒïœÄŒµŒæŒµœÅŒ≥Œ±œÉŒØŒ±
ALTER TABLE books AUTO_INCREMENT = 1;
ALTER TABLE authors AUTO_INCREMENT = 1;
ALTER TABLE customers AUTO_INCREMENT = 1;
ALTER TABLE cart_items AUTO_INCREMENT = 1;
ALTER TABLE book_authors AUTO_INCREMENT = 1;
üîê Important Notes
Never DELETE without understanding dependencies if foreign keys are not set to ON DELETE CASCADE.

Use TRUNCATE TABLE table_name; for faster complete clears only when no FK constraints exist.

Œ§Œø ChatGPT ŒµŒØœÄŒµ:
To fully reset your database tables ‚Äî including deleting all data and resetting the auto-incrementing id values back to 1 ‚Äî you can combine DELETE statements with ALTER TABLE for each table:

‚úÖ Full SQL Reset Script (with ID auto-increment reset)
sql
ŒëŒΩœÑŒπŒ≥œÅŒ±œÜŒÆ
ŒïœÄŒµŒæŒµœÅŒ≥Œ±œÉŒØŒ±
-- Disable safe update mode
SET SQL_SAFE_UPDATES = 0;

-- Delete all rows from dependent tables first
DELETE FROM cart_items;
DELETE FROM book_authors;

-- Then delete from the main entities
DELETE FROM books;
DELETE FROM authors;
DELETE FROM customers;

-- Reset auto-increment counters
ALTER TABLE cart_items AUTO_INCREMENT = 1;
ALTER TABLE book_authors AUTO_INCREMENT = 1;
ALTER TABLE books AUTO_INCREMENT = 1;
ALTER TABLE authors AUTO_INCREMENT = 1;
ALTER TABLE customers AUTO_INCREMENT = 1;

-- Re-enable safe updates (optional)
SET SQL_SAFE_UPDATES = 1;
üìå Notes
‚úÖ DELETE FROM is used instead of TRUNCATE to respect foreign key constraints.

‚úÖ ALTER TABLE ... AUTO_INCREMENT = 1; resets the primary key counter.

‚ö†Ô∏è You must execute these in the order above if foreign key constraints exist (e.g., book_authors references books and authors).

üí° If you're running from a GUI like MySQL Workbench, ensure "Safe Updates" is disabled in Preferences ‚Üí SQL Editor ‚Üí uncheck Safe Updates.

Let me know if you'd like a .sql file for easy import or if you‚Äôre using a specific SQL tool or platform (e.g., DBeaver, MySQL CLI).

Œ§Œø ChatGPT ŒµŒØœÄŒµ:
Great question. Here's the key distinction:

‚úÖ You are correct that:
Using @GeneratedValue(strategy = GenerationType.IDENTITY) in Spring Boot with MySQL will automatically use the database‚Äôs auto-increment feature for the id column. This means:

Yes, IDs are generated by the database.

Yes, inserting the first row into an empty table will likely get id = 1.

‚ùóBUT: MySQL does not automatically reset AUTO_INCREMENT to 1 when you DELETE rows.
üëâ Example:
sql
ŒëŒΩœÑŒπŒ≥œÅŒ±œÜŒÆ
ŒïœÄŒµŒæŒµœÅŒ≥Œ±œÉŒØŒ±
DELETE FROM books;
-- Now insert a new book
-- It might get id = 5 if the last deleted one had id = 4
That‚Äôs because DELETE doesn‚Äôt reset the internal auto-increment counter ‚Äî only TRUNCATE or ALTER TABLE ... AUTO_INCREMENT = 1 will do that.

üîÅ So, when should you use ALTER TABLE ... AUTO_INCREMENT = 1?
‚úÖ When you want to reset IDs (e.g., during development/testing).

‚úÖ When you fully cleared the table and want inserts to start at 1 again.

‚ùå Not needed in production unless you explicitly want it.

üîÑ Summary:
Scenario	Auto-increment resets?	Should use ALTER TABLE?
DELETE FROM table	‚ùå No	‚úÖ Yes
TRUNCATE TABLE table	‚úÖ Yes	‚ùå Optional
Spring Boot with IDENTITY	‚úÖ Uses DB auto-inc	‚ùå Not for ID logic, but maybe for testing

Let me know if you'd like a utility SQL or admin route in Spring Boot to reset data with ID restart.

Invalid username or password! 2025-06-11T17:29:21.046+03:00  INFO 23268 --- [nio-8080-exec-6] c.e.s.controller.CustomerController      : Customer 'admin' is attempting to log in @PostMapping("/login")
public String loginCustomer(@ModelAttribute("customer") Customer customer,
                            HttpServletRequest request,
                            Model model) {
    String username = customer.getUsername();
    String password = customer.getPassword();
    logger.info("Customer '{}' is attempting to log in", username);
    boolean authenticated = customerService.authenticateCustomer(username, password);
    if (authenticated) {
        request.getSession().invalidate();
        HttpSession session = request.getSession(true);
        session.setAttribute("loggedInUser", username);
        Customer loggedIn = customerService.findByUsername(username);
        session.setAttribute("isAdmin", loggedIn.isAdmin());
        logger.info("Customer '{}' logged in successfully", username);
        if (loggedIn.isAdmin()) {
            return "redirect:/admin/books";
        }
        return "redirect:/";
    } else {
        model.addAttribute("customer", new Customer());
        model.addAttribute("error", "Invalid username or password!");
        return "login";
